وإن نكحها صح ولم تصر أم ولده، ويجب مهرها لا قيمتها، وولدها حرّ بقرابته (٤) (1) قوله : ولم تصر أمّ ولده : أي لم تصر أمة الابن المنكوحة أم ولد الأب الناكح إذا ولدت منه وادّعاه لتولده من نكاح ، فلم تبق ضرورة إلى تملكها من وقت العلوق ; لثبوت النسب بدونه. [0]قوله : وولدها حرّ ... الخ ; حاصله : إن الأب إذا تزوج أمةَ الابن، ووُلِدَ منه (۱) «فتح القدير (٣: ٤٠٨).
And if he marries her, it is valid and she does not become umm walad for him, and her mahr is obligatory, not her value, and her child is free due to his kinship. (4) (1) His saying: 'And she does not become umm walad for him' means the son's slave girl who is married does not become umm walad for the father who marries her if she gives birth from him and he claims it, because the birth is from marriage, so there remains no necessity to own her from the time of conception since lineage is established without it. [0] His saying: 'And her child is free...' its summary: The father, if he marries his son's slave girl, and a child is born from him... (1) Fath al-Qadir (3:408).
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This section deals with a different scenario: the father marries his son's slave girl (as a wife, not just intercourse). The ruling is that the marriage is valid. If she gives birth to a child from this marriage, she does not become an umm walad (mother of a free child) for the father, meaning she does not gain the status of being freed upon the father's death, because the child is born from a valid marriage, not from mere intercourse with ownership. Consequently, the father must pay her mahr (dower) as agreed, not her value as in the previous case. The child is free due to the father's paternity (kinship), but the child does not belong to the son; the father is the father. The commentary clarifies that since the birth is from a recognized marriage, there is no need to retroactively establish ownership to preserve lineage, as lineage is already established through marriage. This case contrasts with the earlier case of mere intercourse.

Key Terms
نكاح (nikāḥ): A valid marriage contract between the father and his son's slave girl.
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who bears her master's child; here she does not acquire that status because the child is from marriage, not from ownership.
مهر (mahr): The dower agreed upon in the marriage contract; it is obligatory here because marriage is valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a father marries his son's slave girl and she bears a child, what is the father obligated to pay?
A) Her value (qimah)
B) Her mahr (dower)
C) Neither
D) Half her value

Key Takeaway
A valid marriage contract transforms obligations: the father pays mahr, the woman does not become umm walad, and the child is free through paternity.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on a Father's Union with His Son's Slave-Girl
Explaining the legal effects of a father's union with his son's slave-girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the status of the child born from a father's union with his son's slave-girl and explain the conditions and legal consequences.

Core Idea
The child is free due to kinship, and no compensation is owed for the child.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya, a commentary on al-Wiqayah, presents a fiqh ruling with proof regarding a father's marriage or intercourse with his son's slave-girl. It clarifies the child's freedom, the grandfather's analogous rule, and the financial obligations involved. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to the conditions of ownership and the hadith cited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario and ruling
The passage addresses when a father marries or has intercourse with his son's slave-girl. The key ruling: the child born is free (hurr) due to the father's kinship with the child (the child is the son's brother). Additionally, if married, the marriage is valid, mahr is due, and the slave-girl does not become umm walad.
2
Understand the conditions for freedom without compensation
The child is free and no value (qima) is owed to the son only when the slave-girl is solely owned by the son. If she is jointly owned, the father must compensate the co-owners with 'uqr (value) for his share.
Joint ownership scenarios are detailed in the commentary from al-Fath.
3
Examine the grandfather's position
The grandfather (paternal grandfather) is treated like the father only after the father's death or absence of guardianship (insanity, disbelief, slavery). Before death, the grandfather does not have the same authority.
The grandfather's ruling applies only when the father's guardianship is absent.
4
Apply the hadith proof
The child's freedom is based on the hadith: 'Whoever owns a close blood relative (dhu rahim mahram) becomes free.' The child is a mahram relative (brother) to the son, and the father owns the child (since the child is born in his ownership), so the child is freed. The hadith is narrated by al-Nasa'i, Ahmad, and others.
The hadith is zanni in both transmission and meaning but is operative here.
5
Distinguish between marriage and mere intercourse
If the father marries the slave-girl, the marriage is valid, mahr is obligatory, but she does not become umm walad. If he only has intercourse without marriage, the child is still free, but no mahr is due; however, if the slave-girl is co-owned, 'uqr is required.
The commentary from al-Muhit emphasizes that the child's lineage is established without needing ownership from conception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا قيمة ولدها، والجد كالأب بعد موته فيه لا قبله، وإن نكحها صح ولم تصر أم ولده، ويجب مهرها لا قيمتها، وولدها حر بقرابته

(ولا قيمة ولدها)؛ لأنه وُلِدَ في ملك الأب.

(والجد كالأب بعد موته فيه): أي بعد موت الأب في الحكم المذكور. (لا قبله): أي لا قبل موت الأب.

(وإن نكحها صح): أي إن نكح الأب أمة الابن، ولم تصر أم ولديه. (ويجب مهرها لا قيمتها، وولدها حر بقرابته)

[١] قوله: ولا قيمة ولدها؛ أي لا يجب عليه أداء قيمة الابن المولود من وطئه إلى ابنه، كما في ولد المغرور؛ لأنه عَلِقَ حراً؛ لتقدم الملك، وهذا إذا لم تكن الأمة مشتركة، فإن كانت مشتركة بين ابنه وبين الأجنبي يضمن لشريكه نصف عقرها. وإن كانت مشتركة بين الأب والابن أو غيره تجب حصة الشريك الابن أو غيره من العقر، وقيمة باقيها إذا حبلت؛ لعدم تقدُّم الملك في كلها لانتفاء موجبه، وهو صيانة النسل؛ إذ ما فيها من الملك يكفي لصحة الاستيلاد، وإذا صح ثبت الملك في باقيها حكماً. كذا في «الفتح».

[٢] قوله: والجد؛ والمراد به الجد الصحيح كأب الأب، فخرج به الجد الفاسد كأب الأم، وكذا غير الجد من ذي رحم محرم، فلا يصدقون في جميع الأحوال؛ لفقد [؟] ولا يتهم. كذا في «المحيط». وإنما كان الجد كالأب؛ لأن الشارع جعله كالأب في كثير من الأحكام، وهذا عند عدم ولاية الأب بأن مات أو جن أو كفر أو كان رقيقاً لا عند تحقق ولايته؛ إذ لا حكم للنائب عند وجود الأصل.

(٣) قوله: في الحكم المذكور؛ فإن وطئ الجد جارية ابن ابنه فولدت فادّعاه ثبت نسبه وصارت أم ولد له، ووجبت عليه قيمتها.

(٤) قوله: ولم تصر أم ولده: أي لم تصر أمة الابن المنكوحة أم ولد الأب الناكح إذا ولدت منه وادّعاه لتولده من نكاح، فلم تبق ضرورة إلى تملكها من وقت العلوق؛ لثبوت النسب بدونه.

[٠] قوله: وولدها حر... الخ؛ حاصله: إن الأب إذا تزوج أمة الابن، ووُلِدَ منه

أي بقرابة الابن، فإن الأمة ملك الابن فيتبعها الولد، فيعتق على أخيه، لقوله: من ملك ذا رحم محرم منه عتق عليه.

[١] قوله: ذا رحم؛ الرحم – بالفتح –: القرابة. والمَحرَم - بفتح الميم والراء المهملة، بينهما حاء مهملة ساكنة -: من يحرم نكاحه على سبيل التأبيد، واحترز بهذين القيدين عما إذا ملك رجل ابن عمه، فإنه لا يعتق عليه، فإنه وإن كان ذا رحم لكنه ليس بمحرم، وإذا ملك الرجل أم امرأته لا يعتق عليه؛ لأن المحرمية وإن وجدت لكن لم يوجد الرحم. وسيأتي تفصيل هذه المباحث في «كتاب العتق» إن شاء الله تعالى.

[٢] قوله: عتق؛ أي صار المملوك معتقاً على المالك، وهذا الحديث أخرجه النسائي من حديث ابن عمر، وعند أحمد وأصحاب السنن من حديث سمرة بلفظ: «من ملك ذا رحم محرم فهو حر».
And no value of her child, and the grandfather is like the father after his death in this, not before. And if he married her, it is valid, and she does not become umm walad for him, and her mahr is obligatory, not her value, and her child is free due to his kinship.

(And no value of her child) because he was born in the father's ownership.

(And the grandfather is like the father after his death in this): meaning after the death of the father in the mentioned ruling. (Not before): meaning not before the father's death.

(And if he married her, it is valid): meaning if the father married his son's slave-girl, she does not become his umm walad. (And her mahr is obligatory, not her value, and her child is free due to his kinship)

[1] His saying: 'And no value of her child'; meaning he is not obligated to pay the value of the son born from his intercourse to his son, as in the case of the child of the deceived (al-maghrur), because he became free due to prior ownership of the mother. This is when the slave-girl is not jointly owned. If she is jointly owned between his son and a stranger, he guarantees half of her 'uqr to his partner. And if she is jointly owned between the father and the son or others, the share of the partner (son or other) from the 'uqr is obligatory, and the value of the remainder if she becomes pregnant, due to lack of prior complete ownership, the reason being preservation of lineage, because the partial ownership suffices for the validity of istilad, and if established, ownership of the remainder is established by legal fiction. As in al-Fath.

[2] His saying: 'And the grandfather'; and by it is meant the true grandfather like the paternal grandfather, thus excluded is the false grandfather like the maternal grandfather, and also other than the grandfather from among mahram relatives. So they are not truthful in all cases due to lack [؟] and he is not accused. As in al-Muhit. And the grandfather is like the father because the Lawgiver made him like the father in many rulings. This is when the father's guardianship is absent, such as if he died, or became insane, or disbelieved, or was a slave, not when his guardianship is existent, because there is no ruling for the substitute when the original exists.

(3) His saying: 'in the mentioned ruling'; for if the grandfather had intercourse with the slave-girl of his son's son (i.e., great-grandson) and she gave birth and he claimed the child, his lineage is established, she becomes his umm walad, and he must pay her value.

(4) His saying: 'And she does not become his umm walad': meaning the slave-girl of the son who is married does not become the umm walad of the father who married her if she gives birth from him and he claims the child, because the child is from marriage, so there is no need to own her from the time of conception, since lineage is established without it.

[0] His saying: 'And her child is free... etc.'; the summary: If the father marries his son's slave-girl and a child is born from him... i.e., due to the son's kinship, for the slave-girl is owned by the son, so the child follows her, and thus becomes free relative to his brother, because of his saying: 'Whoever owns a close blood relative (dhu rahim mahram) from him, that relative is freed.'

[1] His saying: 'dhu rahim'; ar-rahim (with fatha) means kinship. Al-mahram (with fat-ha on the mim and ra, with a silent ha between them) is one whose marriage is perpetually prohibited. Two restrictions are intended: if a man owns his paternal cousin, he is not freed upon him, because although he is a relative, he is not a mahram; and if a man owns the mother of his wife, he is not freed upon him because mahramiyya exists but kinship (raham) does not. The details of these topics will come in Kitab al-Itq, insha-Allah.

[2] His saying: 'freed'; meaning the owned person becomes free from the owner. This hadith was narrated by al-Nasa'i from Ibn Umar, and by Ahmad and the authors of the Sunan from Samurah with the wording: 'Whoever owns a close blood relative (dhu rahim mahram) is free.'
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the hadith. It addresses the situation where a father has intercourse with his son's slave-girl. The key points: (1) The child born from such union is free because it is born in the father's ownership and is a close relation to the son (being his brother). (2) If the father marries her (not just intercourse), the marriage is valid, but she does not become umm walad—meaning she does not gain the right to freedom upon the father's death; instead, her mahr is due. (3) The grandfather is treated like the father in these rulings only after the father's death, not during his lifetime. (4) If the slave-girl is jointly owned, different rules apply: the father must pay compensation to the co-owner. The proof for the child's freedom is the hadith 'Whoever owns a close blood relative, that relative becomes free.' The commentary clarifies that 'dhu rahim mahram' includes only those with both blood relation and perpetual marriage prohibition; e.g., a paternal cousin is not freed because not mahram, and the mother of a wife is not freed because no blood relation.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm al-walad): A slave-girl who bears a child to her master and thus becomes free upon his death.
ذي رحم محرم (dhu rahim mahram): A close blood relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited.
عقر ('uqr): Compensation paid to the owner of a slave-girl for sexual access (often equivalent to her value).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the status of a child born from a father's union with his son's slave-girl?
A) The child is a slave of the father.
B) The child is free due to kinship with the son.
C) The child is a slave of the son.
D) The child is free only if the father married the slave-girl.

Key Takeaway
A child born from a father's union with his son's slave-girl is free, and the father owes no compensation for the child, but must pay mahr if married and compensation if the slave-girl is co-owned.
